43:1714:133965:16:17:91:523:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:NELS 8thgraders.  Because the population mean for college enrollment is below 0.5,  the probit
43:1715:134059:17:16:91:523:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:model implies that more disadvantaged subpopulations have fewer students near the decision mar-
43:1716:134154:16:16:91:523:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:gin, so that the largest impacts occur for the most advantaged subgroup (in this case, white students
43:1717:134255:16:17:91:523:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with two college-graduate parents) and the lowest value is for the most disadvantaged subgroup
43:1718:134349:17:16:91:523:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(children of single white mothers with education less than or equal to high school).  The impacts
43:1719:134446:16:17:91:523:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the “School and CZ” treatment on the enrollment probability range from 0.116 to 0.213.  The
43:1720:134540:17:16:91:523:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“School only” treatment displays slightly higher effects than the “CZ only” treatments with similar
43:1721:134639:16:17:91:523:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:degrees of heterogeneity: impacts range from 0.086 to 0.154 for “School only” and 0.075 to 0.142
43:1722:134735:17:16:91:523:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the “CZ only” treatment. The estimates of the treatment effects for the ELS ZIP code and block
43:1723:134833:16:16:91:523:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:group specifications follow the same pattern as in NELS, although the subgroup estimates fall in a
43:1724:134931:16:20:91:160:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:narrower range.
43:1725:134946:20:16:107:523:325:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Figure 3 shows the relationship between the treatment effects on college attendance probability
43:1726:135041:16:17:91:524:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the quantiles ofXXXiBBB.The impact of the counterfactual treatments is non-monotonic inXXXiBBB,
43:1727:135140:17:16:91:523:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:increasing and then decreasing as one moves through the distribution ofXXXiBBB. For example, for the
43:1728:135240:16:16:91:523:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“School and CZ” counterfactual in NELS, the estimated impact for the 10th, 75th(near the maximum
43:1729:135336:16:20:91:423:260:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:impact), and 90thquantiles ofXXXiBBBare 0.062, 0.253, and 0.218, respectively.
43:1730:135414:20:16:107:523:240:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The pattern occurs despite the fact that in the NELS case the coefficient on the interaction be-
43:1731:135510:16:17:91:524:224:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:tweenXXXiBBBandZZZS2sGGGS2is  substantial:  -0.069  (0.034).   Part  of  the  decline  at  the  top  of  theXXXiBBB
43:1732:135625:17:16:91:523:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:distribution may be due to this.  However, the pattern is primarily due to a striking fact about the
43:1733:135725:16:16:91:523:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variation in predicted outcome probabilities acrossXXXiBBBquantiles that is established in Figure 1a.
43:1734:135826:16:17:91:523:175:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In NELS (solid light line) for a school/CZ combination of median quality, the predicted enrollment
43:1735:135924:17:16:91:523:158:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rates for a student at the 10th,  30th,  70thand 90thquantiles ofXXXiBBBare 0.042,  0.136,  0.429,  and
43:1736:136027:16:17:91:523:142:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:0.703,  respectively.  The figure demonstrates just how strongly observed family background and
43:1737:136122:17:16:91:523:125:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:student aptitude measures (as of 8thgrade) predict enrollment at a four-year postsecondary insti-
43:1738:136219:16:0:91:523:109:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tution.  Consequently, very few students near the bottom of theXXXiBBBdistribution are in a position
44:1739:136321:0:16:91:523:732:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:where higher quality school inputs would be enough to push them over the decision margin, even if
44:1740:136418:16:19:91:413:716:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they are slightly more sensitive to school quality than the average student.
44:1741:136494:19:17:107:523:697:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In fact, the ELS ZIP code specification provides a good opportunity to assess the importance
44:1742:136586:17:16:91:524:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the interaction terms in the model.  First,̂sd(ZZZC2cGGGC2)))is substantial, so that there is more signal
44:1743:136694:16:17:91:523:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contained in this regression index with which to identify true interactions.  Second, the interaction
44:1744:136795:17:16:91:523:647:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:coefficients  on  1(LowInc)×ZZZC2cGGGC2and  1(U RM)×ZZZC2cGGGC2are  seemingly  non-negligible  in  size
44:1745:136898:16:17:91:523:631:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(albeit still noisily estimated): 0.050 and 0.054 respectively (Table 4 Panel B).  This suggests greater
44:1746:137002:17:16:91:523:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sensitivity of students from modest backgrounds and minority students to CZ inputs.  Third,  the
44:1747:137098:16:16:91:523:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:variance components for the “CZ only” treatment,Var(ZZZC2cGGGC2+vc), contribute 1.26% ofVar(Yi)
44:1748:137193:16:17:91:524:582:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:when interactions are included and 1.24% ofVar(Yi)when they are excluded.  This means that we
44:1749:137286:17:16:91:523:565:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:can directly compare treatment effects based on the models with and without interactions essentially
44:1750:137386:16:17:91:523:549:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:holding fixed the importance of the main effects. Indeed, the mean impact of the 10th-90th“CZ only”
44:1751:137485:17:19:91:331:532:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:treatment on ENROLL is 0.118 for both specifications.
44:1752:137538:19:16:107:523:513:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:As it turns out,  none of the subgroups we consider displays more than a 0.002 difference in
44:1753:137630:16:17:91:523:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:treatment  effects  between  the  linear  and  non-linear  specification.   While  the  imprecision  of  our
44:1754:137738:17:16:91:523:480:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interaction  estimates  cautions  against  overinterpreting  the  results,  our  limited  evidence  suggests
44:1755:137846:16:17:91:523:464:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that the probit function seems to be doing an effective job of capturing heterogeneity in sensitivity
44:1756:137947:17:33:91:321:447:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to higher quality school and commuting zone inputs.
44:1757:137998:33:23:91:311:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:8.3    Graduation from a Four-Year College
44:1758:138040:23:17:107:523:391:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Panel C of Table 5 reports the estimated impacts of the same counterfactual treatments on a
44:1759:138131:17:16:91:523:374:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:randomly selected student’s probability of graduating college by age 25. The NELS results indicate
44:1760:138229:16:17:91:523:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that replacing a combined school/commuting zone at the 10thquantile of the quality distribution
44:1761:138324:17:16:91:524:341:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with one at the 90thquantile increases the college graduation probability by 0.085 (0.016) (from
44:1762:138420:16:17:91:523:325:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:B:0.309 to 0.394).  Shifting only school inputs or only CZ inputs from their respective 10thto 90th
44:1763:138517:17:16:91:523:308:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quantiles increases the graduation probability by 0.077 (0.18) and 0.046 (0.019), respectively.  The
44:1764:138617:16:16:91:523:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:small increase in impact from shifting school and CZ quality together relative to the impact of the
44:1765:138716:16:17:91:524:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:separate shifts is partly due to an estimated small negative covariance betweenZZZS2sGGGS2andZZZC2cGGGC2.
44:1766:138821:17:7:91:523:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:It also reflects the fact that doubling a variance only increases the standard deviation by a factor of
44:1767:138924:7:9:91:100:252:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:C:√
44:1768:138925:9:20:100:108:243:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:2.
44:1769:138927:20:16:107:523:223:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The ELS block group estimates are only 0.090 (0.012), 0.071 (0.015), and 0.073 (0.017), respec-
44:1770:139022:16:16:91:523:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tively, with the ELS ZIP code estimates displaying slightly smaller magnitudes. Switching from the
44:1771:139120:16:17:91:523:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:full specification to the basic specification (displayed in Online Appendix Table B9) increases the
44:1772:139219:17:19:91:273:174:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates for each dataset by about 0.015.
44:1773:139261:19:17:107:523:155:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The three treatments have a smaller effect on the college graduation probability than the enroll-
44:1774:139358:17:16:91:523:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ment rate. We do not have a complete explanation for this, but three possibilities are worth mention-
44:1775:139459:16:17:91:523:122:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ing.  First, School and CZ inputs may play a bigger role in inducing students to attend a four-year
44:1776:139558:17:0:91:523:105:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:college than to successfully complete college. The second and related point is that marginal students
45:1777:139661:0:16:91:523:732:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:who are induced to enroll in a four-year college as a result of superior school and CZ inputs may
45:1778:139758:16:17:91:523:716:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:graduate at lower rates.  Finally, there is considerable attrition in the sample between the survey in
45:1779:139860:17:16:91:523:699:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which ENROLL is measured (2nd and 3rd Follow-ups for NELS and ELS, respectively) and the
45:1780:139948:16:16:91:523:683:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:survey in which COLLBA is measured (3rd and 4th follow-ups).  Differential attrition could lead
45:1781:140043:16:17:91:523:667:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the sample of students remaining when COLLBA is measured to be less sensitive to school and CZ
45:1782:140137:17:32:91:230:650:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:B:inputs than in earlier samples.39
45:1783:140170:32:24:91:340:618:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:8.3.1    Subpopulation Results for College Graduation
45:1784:140223:24:16:107:523:594:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Table 6 reveals moderate heterogeneity in estimated impacts from the counterfactual treatments
45:1785:140317:16:17:91:524:578:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:across subgroups for NELS 8thgraders.  A 10th-to-90thshift in combined school/CZ input quality
45:1786:140411:17:16:91:523:561:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:increases the probability of college graduation by between 0.056 (0.011) and 0.101 (0.018) with the
45:1787:140510:16:17:91:523:545:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:smallest impacts occurring for white students with a single mother with a high school degree or less
45:1788:140610:17:19:91:419:528:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the largest for white students with two parents with bachelor’s degrees.
45:1789:140686:19:16:107:523:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The variance components attributed to school inputs (Var(ZZZS2sGGGS2)andVar(vs−vc)) are substan-
45:1790:140782:16:17:91:523:493:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tially larger in NELS than those attributed to CZ inputs (Var(ZZZC2cGGGC2)andVar(vc)).  As a result,
45:1791:140882:17:16:91:523:476:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the counterfactual impacts are substantially larger for the “School only” specification than the “CZ
45:1792:140982:16:17:91:524:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:only” specification, particularly for subgroups featuring high values ofXXXiBBB.  For example, a 10th-
45:1793:141084:17:16:91:523:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to-90thquantile shift in the quality of school inputs increases enrollment by 0.081 for the white
45:1794:141181:16:17:91:523:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:subpopulation,  while the corresponding shift in the quality of commuting zone inputs only pro-
45:1795:141276:17:16:91:523:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:duces a 0.049 increase. The “School Only” and “CZ Only” treatment effects are much more similar
45:1796:141371:16:19:91:171:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to another in ELS.
45:1797:141389:19:17:107:523:375:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Once again, examining the variation in treatment impacts acrossXXXiBBBquantiles reveals a greater
45:1798:141486:17:16:91:524:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:degree of heterogeneity (Figure 4).   For NELS, the “School and CZ” impacts for the 10th,  75th,
45:1799:141582:16:17:91:523:342:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and 90thquantiles ofXXXiBBBare 0.031, 0.124, and 0.098, respectively, demonstrating the same non-
45:1800:141679:17:16:91:523:325:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:monotonicity of treatment effects across theXXXiBBBdistribution as was observed for the college en-
45:1801:141778:16:16:91:523:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rollment outcome. Figure 1a shows that in NELS the probability of college graduation is 0.046 for
45:1802:141875:16:17:91:524:293:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a student at the 10thquantile ofXXXiBBBand 0.754 at the 90th(evaluated at the median value of the
45:1803:141972:17:33:91:216:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“School and CZ” treatment).
45:1804:141999:33:23:91:201:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:8.4    Log Wage Rates
45:1805:142020:23:17:107:523:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Columns 10-12 of Table 5 report the estimated impacts of the same counterfactual treatments on
45:1806:142114:17:16:91:523:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a randomly selected student’s log wage as of about age 25. The NELS results (col. 10) indicate that
45:1807:142213:16:17:91:524:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the effect of the 10th-90thquantile combined school/commuting zone treatment is 0.111 (0.025) log
45:1808:142310:17:16:91:523:170:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:points (which corresponds to an 11.7% wage increase).  A one standard deviation improvement in
45:1809:142404:16:17:91:523:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the treatment would raise log wages by 0.045 (a 4.6% wage increase). In comparison, the standard
45:1810:142500:17:17:91:523:137:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:deviation of the permanent component of the wage is 0.361. The values for ELS are slightly smaller.
45:1811:142599:17:14:103:523:120:7:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:39As discussed in Section 5, the mean of ENROLL among sample members of the 3rd follow-up survey in NELS
45:1812:142703:14:11:91:523:106:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:is  .353  vs.   .327  among  those  in  the  2nd  follow-up  (when  the  outcome  is  determined),  suggesting  some  differential
45:1813:142833:11:0:91:184:95:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:attribution is taking place.
46:1814:142863:0:16:91:523:732:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  estimate  of  the  combined  school/community  10th-90thtreatment  effect  is  only  .104  (0.024)
46:1815:142966:16:17:91:523:716:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:log  points  in  the  block  group  specification  (an  11%  wage  increase).   Estimates  using  the  basic
46:1816:143074:17:19:91:351:699:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specification in Online Appendix Table B9 are very similar.
46:1817:143133:19:16:107:523:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The effect of the 10th-90thcommuting zone treatment is larger than the school treatment in both
46:1818:143228:16:17:91:523:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:NELS and in ELS, in contrast to what we found for education. One would expect commuting zone
46:1819:143320:17:16:91:523:647:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:characteristics to be particularly important for wages, where opportunities in the local labor market
46:1820:143421:16:19:91:156:631:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are paramount.
46:1821:143435:19:17:107:523:612:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Since the wage model is linear, the only source of treatment effect heterogeneity consists of the
46:1822:143532:17:16:91:524:595:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interaction terms betweenMMMiandZZZS2sGGGS2andZZZC2cGGGC2. The coefficients on the interactions terms are
46:1823:143637:16:33:91:337:579:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:small, so we do not find important subgroup differences.
46:1824:143693:33:24:91:362:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:8.5    Summary of Results from Counterfactual Shifts
46:1825:143745:24:16:107:523:522:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:A:There are several broad takeaways from the estimated impacts of counterfactual 10th-to-90th
46:1826:143836:16:17:91:523:506:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quantile shifts in school and/or commuting zone inputs. First, large changes in school and commut-
46:1827:143934:17:19:91:463:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ing zone inputs can make a substantial difference in students’ educational attainment.
46:1828:144020:19:17:107:523:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Second, the impact of these inputs is quite heterogeneous across disadvantaged vs. advantaged
46:1829:144113:17:16:91:523:453:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:students.  The dropout rates of disadvantaged students are particularly sensitive to the external en-
46:1830:144214:16:16:91:523:437:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:vironment, while few advantaged students are near the margin.  In contrast, for college enrollment
46:1831:144312:16:17:91:523:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and graduation, superior school and commuting zone inputs are important for all, but particularly
46:1832:144409:17:16:91:523:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:consequential for students near (or above) the middle of the distribution of student and family back-
46:1833:144510:16:20:91:125:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ground.
46:1834:144517:20:16:107:523:368:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Third,  the more general model featuring interactions between student and school/commuting
46:1835:144607:16:16:91:523:352:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:zone inputs produces predicted impacts of shifts in school and commuting zone environment that
46:1836:144701:16:17:91:523:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:differ little from the results using the simpler probit specification without interactions. This suggests
46:1837:144806:17:16:91:523:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that the nonlinearity inherent in the probit function does a fairly good job of capturing differential
46:1838:144908:16:17:91:523:303:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sensitivity to school and region-level inputs, and that a linear specification for the probit index may
46:1839:145011:17:16:91:523:286:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:suffice in similar contexts.  But this need not be true in other applications and the estimates of the
46:1840:145113:16:19:91:254:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interaction coefficients are imprecise.
46:1841:145152:19:17:107:523:251:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Finally,  both school and commuting zone inputs seem to be important, and with comparable
46:1842:145241:17:16:91:523:234:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:magnitudes.  However, this conclusion is more tentative, because we cannot fully distinguish be-
46:1843:145337:16:39:91:425:218:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tween unobservable school inputs and unobservable commuting zone inputs.
46:1844:145409:39:28:91:181:179:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:9    Conclusion
46:1845:145424:28:16:107:523:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Educational attainment and wages, like many adult outcomes, are influenced by factors that are
46:1846:145518:16:17:91:523:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specific to the individual as well as aspects of the broader social environment. In this paper, we build
46:1847:145622:17:16:91:523:118:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the rich literature on sorting, school and neighborhood effects, and multilevel modeling to assess
46:1848:145723:16:0:91:523:102:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the relative importance of neighborhood, school, and broader local area factors in shaping student’s
47:1849:145825:0:16:91:523:732:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:educational attainment and early career wages,  and the degree to which this relative importance
47:1850:145921:16:17:91:523:716:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:differs across students from different backgrounds.  We extend the identification results of Altonji
47:1851:146021:17:16:91:523:699:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Mansfield (2018) to models with multiple group levels and with interactions between observed
47:1852:146117:16:16:91:523:683:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individual factors and both observed and unobserved group level factors. The identification results
47:1853:146216:16:17:91:523:667:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are based on the idea that group averages of individual-level observables can fully control for sorting
47:1854:146319:17:16:91:523:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bias from group averages of individual-level unobservables. A natural but challenging extension to
47:1855:146417:16:20:91:493:634:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our analysis would be to incorporate interactions with unobserved individual characteristics.
47:1856:146510:20:16:107:523:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our theoretical results demonstrate the existence of a structural decomposition of variation in
47:1857:146605:16:16:91:523:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:educational and labor market outcomes of interest into four components:  (1) individual contribu-
47:1858:146702:16:17:91:523:582:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tions that are common across groups, (2) group contributions that are common across individuals,
47:1859:146798:17:16:91:523:565:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(3)  contributions  that  consist  of  interactions  between  student  and  group  inputs,  and  a  (4)  set  of
47:1860:146910:16:17:91:523:549:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ambiguous contributions, absorbed by our control function of group-level averages, that reflect a
47:1861:147007:17:19:91:435:532:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:combination of common group inputs and group-averages of individual inputs.
47:1862:147082:19:16:107:523:513:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We implement this structural decomposition using a multilevel mixed effects model, and use the
47:1863:147176:16:17:91:523:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:results to generate lower bound estimates of the average impact among the student population of
47:1864:147271:17:16:91:523:480:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“treatments” consisting of shifts in school, commuting zone, and combined school/commuting zone
47:1865:147366:16:17:91:523:464:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quality from the 10thto the 90thquantile of their respective distributions. We also produce estimates
47:1866:147467:17:16:91:523:447:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for particular student subpopulations that exploit the treatment effect heterogeneity accommodated
47:1867:147565:16:19:91:152:431:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by our model.
47:1868:147578:19:17:107:523:412:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Despite accounting for a small share of the total variance in the latent indices that generate our
47:1869:147676:17:16:91:523:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:binary outcomes, our population average estimates suggest that school and commuting zone inputs
47:1870:147771:16:17:91:523:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:play an important role in determining educational attainment.  Moving from a school/commuting
47:1871:147864:17:16:91:524:362:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:zone combination at the 10thquality quantile to a 90thquantile combination increases the probability
47:1872:147964:16:17:91:523:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of high school graduation by at least 0.06-0.09 across datasets and specifications, the probability of
47:1873:148066:17:16:91:523:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:enrollment at a four-year college by at least 0.17-0.18, and the probability of college graduation by at
47:1874:148170:16:17:91:523:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:least 0.08-0.09. School and commuting zone inputs seem to play a roughly equal role in producing
47:1875:148266:17:16:91:523:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:educational attainment, though the model’s ability to distinguish between the two is more limited.
47:1876:148364:16:16:91:523:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:A 10th-90thquantile shift in school/commuting zone quality increases wages by 10-11 percent, with
47:1877:148461:16:20:91:498:264:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:commuting zone factors playing a somewhat larger role relative to school inputs and policies.
47:1878:148554:20:16:107:523:244:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:High school graduation rates of disadvantaged populations are considerably more sensitive to
47:1879:148646:16:17:91:523:228:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:school  and  commuting  zone  inputs,  while  college  graduation  rates  are  more  sensitive  to  group-
47:1880:148752:17:16:91:523:211:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:level inputs for advantaged populations.  However, the heterogeneity in treatment effects is driven
47:1881:148851:16:16:91:523:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by the share of the subpopulation near the decision margin in our probit models,  rather than by
47:1882:148947:16:17:91:523:179:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fundamental  differences  in  input  sensitivity.   Our  estimated  interaction  effects  are  usually  small
47:1883:149056:17:16:91:523:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(though somewhat imprecise), suggesting that the inherent nonlinearity in the probit model well-
47:1884:149152:16:20:91:443:146:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:approximates the heterogeneity in school and commuting zone treatment effects.
47:1885:149230:20:16:107:523:126:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our  analysis  of  a  regression  index  of  student-level  observables  suggests  that  most  outcome-
47:1886:149333:16:0:91:523:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relevant sorting takes place at the level of school attendance zones, with a modest role for commut-
48:1887:149435:0:16:91:523:732:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ing zone-level sorting and a very small role for neighborhood sorting.  It is possible, of course, that
48:1888:149538:16:17:91:523:716:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the neighborhood component may be understated by the use of block group or ZIP code to define
48:1889:149631:17:19:91:205:699:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:neighborhood boundaries.
48:1890:149655:19:16:107:523:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:While the panel surveys we use offer many advantages, a multilevel mixed effects model fea-
48:1891:149746:16:17:91:523:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:turing interactions among multiple combinations of levels places strong demands on the data. This
48:1892:149843:17:16:91:523:647:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:leads some of our estimates (particularly interactions) to be imprecise, and highlights the value of
48:1893:149943:16:17:91:523:631:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:increasingly available linked administrative data that offer both many groups at each hierarchical
48:1894:150041:17:16:91:523:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:level and large numbers of individuals per group, along with rich sets of observable characteris-
48:1895:150138:16:16:91:523:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tics at each level.  Obtaining observed neighborhood characteristics that are plausible sources of
48:1896:150236:16:0:91:376:582:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:neighborhood-level causal effects would be particularly valuable.
